<p><b>Prince Henry of Wales</b> (Henry Charles Albert David;<sup id="cite_ref-sur_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sur-1"><span>[</span>fn 1<span>]</span></a></sup> born 15 September 1984), known as <b>Prince Harry</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> is the younger son of <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>. His paternal grandparents are <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a>. Prince Harry is the fourth in the <a href="/wiki/Line_of_succession_to_the_British_throne" title="Line of succession to the British throne">Line of succession to the British throne</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Prince_George_of_Cambridge" title="Prince George of Cambridge">Prince George of Cambridge</a>, the only child of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Duke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Cambridge" title="Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge">Duchess of Cambridge</a>.</p>
<p>After an education at schools in the United Kingdom and spending parts of his <a href="/wiki/Gap_year" title="Gap year">gap year</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, Harry chose a military career, undergoing officer training at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military Academy Sandhurst">Royal Military Academy Sandhurst</a>. He was commissioned as a <a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Blues_and_Royals" title="Blues and Royals">Blues and Royals</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Household_Cavalry_Regiment" title="Household Cavalry Regiment">Household Cavalry Regiment</a>, serving temporarily with his brother, and completed his training as a troop leader. In 2007–2008 he <a href="/wiki/Operation_Herrick" title="Operation Herrick">served for 77 days</a> in Helmand, Afghanistan<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> but he was pulled out following publication of the story in an Australian magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He returned to Afghanistan for a 20-week deployment in 2012–2013 with the <a href="/wiki/Army_Air_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Air Corps (United Kingdom)">Army Air Corps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bigstory.ap.org_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigstory.ap.org-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Military_career"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Military career</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Harry was born at <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Hospital,_London" title="St Mary's Hospital, London">St Mary's Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paddington" title="Paddington">Paddington</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England, on 15 September 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-ten16sep_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ten16sep-6"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He was baptised on 21 December 1984 at <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel_at_Windsor_Castle" title="St George's Chapel at Windsor Castle" class="mw-redirect">St George's Chapel at Windsor Castle</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Runcie" title="Robert Runcie">Robert Runcie</a>. His godparents were the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Duke of York</a> (his paternal uncle), <a href="/wiki/Lady_Sarah_Chatto" title="Lady Sarah Chatto">Lady Sarah Armstrong-Jones</a> (his paternal cousin once removed), Lady Celia Vestey (née Knight), Carolyn Bartholomew (née Pride), <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Organ" title="Bryan Organ">Bryan Organ</a> and Gerald Ward (former officer in the Household Cavalry).<sup id="cite_ref-Yvonne_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yvonne-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-peo14jan_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peo14jan-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Diana wanted Harry and his older brother <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">William</a> to have a broader range of experiences than previous royal children and took them to venues that ranged from <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Disney World</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> to AIDS clinics and shelters for the homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry began to accompany his parents on official visits at an early age; his first overseas royal tour was with his parents to Italy in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harry's parents divorced in 1996, and his mother <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Death of Diana, Princess of Wales">died following a car accident</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> the following year. Harry and William were staying with their father at <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral</a> at the time, and the Prince of Wales told his sons about their mother's death.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> At his <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">mother's funeral</a>, Harry, then 12, accompanied his father, brother, paternal grandfather, and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Spencer,_9th_Earl_Spencer" title="Charles Spencer, 9th Earl Spencer">maternal uncle, Earl Spencer</a> in walking behind the funeral cortège from <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a> to <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like his father and brother, Harry was educated at <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Independent school (United Kingdom)">independent schools</a>. He started at Jane Mynors' nursery school and the pre-preparatory <a href="/wiki/Wetherby_School" title="Wetherby School">Wetherby School</a>, both in London.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Following this, he attended <a href="/wiki/Ludgrove_School" title="Ludgrove School">Ludgrove School</a>, and, after passing the entrance exams, was admitted to <a href="/wiki/Eton_College" title="Eton College">Eton College</a>, where he studied geography, art history and art at <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level" title="GCE Advanced Level" class="mw-redirect">A-Level</a>. The decision to place Harry at Eton went against the Windsor family tradition of sending children to <a href="/wiki/Gordonstoun" title="Gordonstoun">Gordonstoun</a> (Harry's grandfather, father, two uncles, and two cousins all attended); it did make Harry follow in the Spencer family footsteps, as both Diana's father and brother had attended Eton.<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2003, Harry completed his education at Eton with two <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Level_(UK)" title="Advanced Level (UK)" class="mw-redirect">A-Levels</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> (achieving a grade B in art and D in geography) having decided to drop history of art after AS level.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> He excelled in sports, particularly <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Passing two A-levels, Harry was eligible to apply for an officer commission in the British Army.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After school, Harry took a <a href="/wiki/Gap_year" title="Gap year">gap year</a>, during which he spent time in Australia, working (as his father had done in his youth) on a cattle station and participating in the Young England vs Young Australia Polo Test Match.<sup id="cite_ref-POWInt_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POWInt-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> He also travelled to <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, where he worked with orphaned children and produced the documentary film <i>The Forgotten Kingdom</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_career">Military career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Military career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inspection-New-Colours.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Inspection-New-Colours.JPG/220px-Inspection-New-Colours.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Inspection-New-Colours.JPG/330px-Inspection-New-Colours.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Inspection-New-Colours.JPG/440px-Inspection-New-Colours.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2242" data-file-height="1495" /></a>

Officer Cadet Wales (standing to attention next to the horse) on parade at Sandhurst, 21 June 2005</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sandhurst.2C_Blues_and_Royals.2C_and_First_Tour_of_Duty_to_Afghanistan">Sandhurst, Blues and Royals, and First Tour of Duty to Afghanistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Sandhurst, Blues and Royals, and First Tour of Duty to Afghanistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Harry entered the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military Academy Sandhurst">Royal Military Academy Sandhurst</a> on 8 May 2005, where he was known as Officer Cadet Wales, and joined the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_Sandhurst#Organisation" title="Royal Military Academy Sandhurst">Alamein Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Within a year, in April 2006, Harry completed his officer training and was commissioned as a <a href="/wiki/Cornet_(military_rank)" title="Cornet (military rank)">Cornet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Blues_and_Royals" title="Blues and Royals">Blues and Royals</a>, a regiment of the <a href="/wiki/Household_Cavalry" title="Household Cavalry">Household Cavalry</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>. He was given the <a href="/wiki/Service_number" title="Service number">service number</a> 564673.<sup id="cite_ref-LG_30_May_2006_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LG_30_May_2006-20"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> On 13 April 2008, when he reached two years' seniority, Harry was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Lieutenant (British Army and Royal Marines)">lieutenant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LG_15_April_2008_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LG_15_April_2008-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">British Ministry of Defence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clarence_House" title="Clarence House">Clarence House</a> made a joint announcement on 22 February 2007 that Harry would be deployed with his regiment to Iraq, as part of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Mechanized_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="1st Mechanized Brigade (United Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect">1st Mechanised Brigade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Mechanised_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="3rd Mechanised Division (United Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect">3rd Mechanised Division</a>&#160;– a move supported by Harry, who had stated that he would leave the army if he was told to remain in safety while his regiment went to war;<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> he said: "There's no way I'm going to put myself through Sandhurst and then sit on my arse back home while my boys are out fighting for their country."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The head of the British army at the time, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dannatt,_Baron_Dannatt" title="Richard Dannatt, Baron Dannatt">General Sir Richard Dannatt</a>, first said on 30 April 2007 that he had personally decided that Harry would serve with his unit in Iraq,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and Harry was scheduled for deployment in May or June 2007, to patrol the <a href="/wiki/Maysan_Province" title="Maysan Province" class="mw-redirect">Maysan Province</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> By 16 May, however, Dannatt announced that Prince Harry would not serve in Iraq;<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> concerns included Harry being a high-value target (as several threats by various groups had already been made against him) and the dangers the soldiers around him would face should any attempt be made on Harry's life or capture. Clarence House made public Harry's disappointment with the decision, though he said he would abide by it.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em;width:315px;float:right;clear:right;border-spacing:2px;font-size:90%">

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Herrick" title="Operation Herrick">Operation Herrick</a></li>
</ul>
</td>

<p>It was reported in early June 2007 that Harry had arrived in Canada to train alongside soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" title="Canadian Forces" class="mw-redirect">Canadian Forces</a> and British Army, at <a href="/wiki/CFB_Suffield" title="CFB Suffield">CFB Suffield</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Medicine_Hat,_Alberta" title="Medicine Hat, Alberta" class="mw-redirect">Medicine Hat, Alberta</a>. It was said that this was in preparation for a <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_duty" title="Tour of duty">tour of duty</a> in Afghanistan, where Canadian and British forces were participating in the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Afghan War</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> rumours that were confirmed in February the following year, when the British Ministry of Defence revealed that Harry had secretly been deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_Air_Controller" title="Forward Air Controller" class="mw-redirect">Forward Air Controller</a> to <a href="/wiki/Helmand_Province" title="Helmand Province">Helmand Province</a> in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The revelation came after the media&#160;– notably, the German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild</a></i> and Australian magazine <i><a href="/wiki/New_Idea" title="New Idea">New Idea</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>&#160;– breached the blackout placed over the information by the Canadian and British authorities. It was later reported that, while in Afghanistan, Harry had helped <a href="/wiki/Brigade_of_Gurkhas" title="Brigade of Gurkhas">Gurkha</a> troops repel an attack from <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> insurgents,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> and performed patrol duty in hostile areas.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> His tour made Harry the first member of the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a> to serve in a war zone since his uncle, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew</a>, flew helicopters during the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>. For his service, Harry was presented with an <a href="/wiki/Operational_Service_Medal_for_Afghanistan" title="Operational Service Medal for Afghanistan">Operational Service Medal for Afghanistan</a> by his aunt, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Combermere_Barracks" title="Combermere Barracks">Combermere Barracks</a> in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleMedal_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleMedal-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Army_Air_Corps_and_Second_Tour_of_Duty_to_Afghanistan">Army Air Corps and Second Tour of Duty to Afghanistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Army Air Corps and Second Tour of Duty to Afghanistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2008, it was announced that Harry was to follow his brother, father and uncle in learning to fly military helicopters. After passing the initial aptitude test, he was to undertake a month-long course; if he passed that, he would begin full flight training in early 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry had to pass his flying assessment at the <a href="/wiki/Army_Air_Corps_Middle_Wallop" title="Army Air Corps Middle Wallop" class="mw-redirect">Army Air Corps Base (AAC), Middle Wallop</a>, the result of which determined if he would pass on to train as a pilot of the <a href="/wiki/Westland_WAH-64_Apache" title="Westland WAH-64 Apache" class="mw-redirect">Apache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westland_Lynx" title="Westland Lynx">Lynx</a>, or <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale_Gazelle" title="Aérospatiale Gazelle">Gazelle</a> helicopter.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Having reached the requisite standard, Harry attended the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Helicopter_Flying_School" title="Defence Helicopter Flying School">Defence Helicopter Flying School</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Shawbury" title="RAF Shawbury">RAF Shawbury</a>, where he joined brother William.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg/170px-Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg/255px-Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg/340px-Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Harry_talks_to_an_injured_soldier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Captain Wales talks to an injured soldier at the <a href="/wiki/Walter_Reed_National_Military_Medical_Center" title="Walter Reed National Military Medical Center">Walter Reed National Military Medical Center</a>, 15 May 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harry was presented with his flying <a href="/wiki/Aircrew_brevet" title="Aircrew brevet">brevet</a> (wings) by his father on 7 May 2010 at a ceremony at the Army Air Corps Base (AAC), Middle Wallop. Harry had let it be known that he intended to fly Apache attack helicopters if he was successful in passing the rigorous Apache training course, after which time it could be possible for him to see active military service once again on the frontline in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Daily_Telegraph_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Daily_Telegraph-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> During the ceremony, he switched his <a href="/wiki/Blues_and_Royals" title="Blues and Royals">Blues and Royals</a>' Officer's <a href="/wiki/British_Army_uniform#No.2:_Service_dress_.28temperate_parade_uniform.29" title="British Army uniform">Service Dress</a> cap for that of the Army Air Corps' sky blue <a href="/wiki/Beret" title="Beret">beret</a> with a Blues and Royals badge.</p>
<p>On 10 March 2011, it was revealed that Harry had passed his Apache flying test and he was awarded his Apache Flying Badge on 14 April 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There was speculation that he would return to Afghanistan before the withdrawal in 2015. On 16 April 2011, it was announced that Harry had been promoted to <a href="/wiki/Captain_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Captain (British Army and Royal Marines)">captain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-captain_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-captain-39"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2011, Clarence House announced that on completion of his training conversion course to use Apache helicopters in the war arena, Harry would be available for deployment, including in current operations in Afghanistan, as an Apache helicopter pilot.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The final decision will ultimately rest with the Ministry of Defence's senior commanders, including principally the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the Defence Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Defence Staff</a> in consultation with the wishes of Harry, the Prince of Wales and the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> In October, Harry was transferred to a US military base in California to complete his helicopter gunship training. This final phase will include live-fire training and "environmental and judgment training" at naval and air force facilities in California and Arizona. The majority of those completing the two-month Apache training are deployed to the front lines in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same month, it was reported that Harry was said to be a natural pilot who was top of his class in the extensive training he had undertaken at the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Facility_El_Centro" title="Naval Air Facility El Centro">Naval Air Facility</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Centro,_California" title="El Centro, California">El Centro, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 2011, Harry returned to England. He went to Wattisham Flying Station in Suffolk, in the east of England, to complete his training to fly Apache helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 September 2012, he arrived at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Bastion" title="Camp Bastion">Camp Bastion</a> in southern Afghanistan as part of the 100-strong <a href="/wiki/Army_Air_Corps_(United_Kingdom)#Regiments" title="Army Air Corps (United Kingdom)">662 Squadron, 3 Regiment, Army Air Corps</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> to begin a four-month combat tour as a co-pilot and gunner for an Apache helicopter.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> This was considered a particular honour as most pilots are required to sit in the "back seat" before being promoted to gunner. On 10 September, within days of arriving in Afghanistan, it was reported that the Taliban threatened his life. Taliban spokesman <a href="/wiki/Zabiullah_Mujahid" title="Zabiullah Mujahid">Zabiullah Mujahid</a> spoke to <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> and was quoted as saying; "We are using all our strength to get rid of him, either by killing or kidnapping," and "We have informed our commanders in Helmand to do whatever they can to eliminate him."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It was announced on 21 January 2013 that Harry was returning from a 20-week deployment in Afghanistan,<sup id="cite_ref-bigstory.ap.org_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigstory.ap.org-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> where he served as an Apache co-pilot/gunner.</p>
<p>On 8 July 2013, the Ministry of Defence announced that Harry had successfully qualified as an Apache aircraft commander.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HQ_London_District_and_Invictus_Games">HQ London District and Invictus Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: HQ London District and Invictus Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 17 January 2014, the Ministry of Defence announced that Harry had completed his attachment to 3 Regiment Army Air Corps and would take up a staff officer role at the position of SO3 (Defence Engagement) in HQ London District. His responsibilities would include helping to co-ordinate significant projects and commemorative events involving the Army in London. He will be based at Horse Guards in central London.<sup id="cite_ref-British_Government_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British_Government-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 March 2014, Prince Harry launched <a href="/wiki/Invictus_Games_(sport)" title="Invictus Games (sport)" class="mw-redirect">Invictus Games</a>, a Paralympic-style sporting event for injured servicemen and women, which is to be held on 10–14 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry met British hopefuls for the Invictus Games at <a href="/wiki/Tedworth_House" title="Tedworth House">Tedworth House</a> for the start of the selection process Invictus Games on 29 April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 May 2014, Harry attended a ticket sale launch for Invictus Games at BT Tower, where he made a public tweet on the Invictus Games official Twitter account as the President of Invictus Games.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In order to promote the Games, Prince Harry was interviewed by <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(presenter)" title="Chris Evans (presenter)">Chris Evans</a> along with two Invictus Games hopefuls, where Prince Harry said: "This (Invictus Games) is basically my full-time job at the moment, making sure that we pull this off." The show aired on 31 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry had written an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> about his experiences at Afghanistan, and how they had inspired him to help the injured personnel, after the trip to the Warrior Games, he vowed to bring Invictus Games to life. The article was published on 10 August 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry and officials attended the British Armed Forces Team announcement for Invictus Games at Potters Field Park on 13 August 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> As President of the Invictus Games, Prince Harry attended the welcome party, driving challenge, and all events related to the Games from 8 to 14 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_duties">Royal duties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Royal duties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg/170px-Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/af/Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/af/Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg 2x" data-file-width="238" data-file-height="297" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Henry_of_Wales.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harry speaking at the press launch for Walking with the Wounded, 1 March 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the age of 21, Harry was appointed as a <a href="/wiki/Counsellor_of_State" title="Counsellor of State">Counsellor of State</a> and began his duties in that capacity when the Queen was attending the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting_2005" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting 2005">2005 Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting</a> in Malta. The following year, Harry was in Lesotho to visit again <a href="/wiki/Msizi_Africa#Mants.27ase_Children.27s_Home" title="Msizi Africa">Mants'ase Children's Home</a> near <a href="/wiki/Mohale%27s_Hoek" title="Mohale's Hoek">Mohale's Hoek</a>, which he first toured in 2004 and, along with <a href="/wiki/Prince_Seeiso_of_Lesotho" title="Prince Seeiso of Lesotho">Prince Seeiso of Lesotho</a>, launched <a href="/wiki/Sentebale" title="Sentebale">Sentebale: The Princes' Fund for Lesotho</a>, a charity to aid children orphaned by HIV/AIDS. He has granted his <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">patronage</a> to organisations including WellChild, Dolen Cymru, and <a href="/wiki/MapAction" title="MapAction">MapAction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> To aid Sentebale, and the <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales_Memorial_Fund" title="Diana, Princess of Wales Memorial Fund">Diana, Princess of Wales Memorial Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centrepoint_(charity)" title="Centrepoint (charity)">Centrepoint</a>, Harry and his brother organised the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, on 1 July 2007.</p>
<p>Sport has been a way that Harry has helped charities and other organisations, such as training as a Rugby Development Officer for the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a> in 2004 and coaching students in schools to encourage them to learn the sport. He has participated in <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a> matches, like his brother and father, to raise money for charitable causes.<sup id="cite_ref-POWInt_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POWInt-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 January 2009, the Queen granted Harry and William their own <a href="/wiki/Royal_Households_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Households of the United Kingdom">royal household</a>. It has three main staff members, supported by a "small" team. Sir <a href="/wiki/David_Manning" title="David Manning">David Manning</a>, the former British ambassador to Washington, is a part-time adviser to the princes. Previously, William and Harry's affairs had been handled by the office of their father at Clarence House in central London. The new household released a statement, complete with their own <a href="/wiki/Monogram" title="Monogram">cyphers</a> at the top, announcing that they have established their own office at nearby <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_Palace" title="St James's Palace">St James's Palace</a> to look after their public, military and charitable activities.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry's cypher is similar to his brother's, but with an <i>H</i> in a shade of blue similar to that used by his mother. In September 2009, William and Harry set up <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Foundation_of_The_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cambridge_and_Prince_Harry" title="The Royal Foundation of The Duke and Duchess of Cambridge and Prince Harry">The Foundation of Prince William and Prince Harry</a> to enable the princes to take forward their charitable ambitions. The foundation is the culmination of the princes' charitable lives so far.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG/170px-Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG" width="170" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG/255px-Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG/340px-Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1430" data-file-height="1648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Harry_Trooping_the_Colour_cropped.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harry at <a href="/wiki/Trooping_the_Colour" title="Trooping the Colour">Trooping the Colour</a>, June 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2012, Harry led an official visit to <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> as part of the Queen's Diamond Jubilee celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> He continued to the Bahamas and Jamaica, where the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Portia_Simpson-Miller" title="Portia Simpson-Miller">Portia Simpson-Miller</a>, is considering severing ties between Jamaica and the constitutional monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> He next visited Brazil to attend the GREAT Campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> as an ambassador of the 2012 Olympics to the 2016 Rio Olympics. On 12 August 2012, Harry represented the Queen at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">Closing Ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">London 2012 Olympic Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From 9 to 15 May 2013, Harry was on an official visit to the United States. The tour promoted the rehabilitation of injured American and UK troops, publicised his own charities and supported British interests. It included engagements in Washington DC, Denver, New York, New Jersey and Connecticut. He watched the opening ceremony of the Warrior Games, in Colorado Springs, where injured servicemen and women competed, and met survivors of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in New Jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2013, Prince Harry visited Australia for his first official visit to the country. Prince Harry attended the International Fleet Review at Sydney Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> He also paid a visit to the Australian SAS HQ in Perth.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> On his way back to UK, he attended a charity event for Sentebale at Dubai.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, Prince Harry visited Estonia and Italy. In Estonia he visited Freedom Square in the capital Tallinn to honour those who paid the ultimate sacrifice for their nation, and attended a reception at the Estonian Parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> and attended Nato military exercise there.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In Italy, Prince Harry attended commemorate the 70th anniversary of Monte Cassino battles for the Polish, Commonwealth and British troops.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry also revealed the British Pavilion at Expo Milano 2015 in Rome at the MAXXI Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014, Prince Harry visited Brazil and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To mark the World War I centenary, on 4 August 2014, Prince Harry attended the unveiling of the Folkestone Memorial Arch in Kent.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Subsequently he flew to Belgium, where he met families of WWI soldiers in a reception before reading a letter from a fallen soldier in a twilight service at St Symphorien Cemetery in Mons.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry and The Duke and Duchess of Cambridge planted poppies at an installation by artist Paul Cummins, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_Swept_Lands_and_Seas_of_Red" title="Blood Swept Lands and Seas of Red">Blood Swept Lands and Seas of Red</a></i> at the Tower of London for commemorations of the war on 5 August.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 November 2014, Prince Harry opened the Field of Remembrance at Westminster Abbey,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> the task usually held by The Duke of Edinburgh. On Nov.7,2013 Prince Harry accompanied The Duke of Edinburgh to open the Field of Remembrance at Westminster Abbey <sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> as Harry's first visit to the event.</p>
<p>On 9 November 2014, Prince Harry attended Remembrance Sunday Service at Kandahar Air Base, Afghanistan, representing HM The Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Prince Harry is patron of the following organisations:<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>WellChild</li>
<li>Walking with the Wounded (2011 North Pole, 2012 Mount Everest, 2013 South Pole)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/HALO_Trust" title="HALO Trust">HALO Trust</a>'s 25th Anniversary Appeal</li>
<li>London Marathon Charitable Trust</li>
<li>MapAction</li>
<li>Dolen Cymru</li>
<li>100 Women in Hedge Funds' Philanthropic Initiatives</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a> (Vice Patron)</li>
<li>Rugby Football Union Injured Players Foundation</li>
<li>Rugby Football Union All Schools Programme</li>
<li>Henry Van Straubenzee Memorial Fund (Joint Patron with his brother)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sentebale" title="Sentebale">Sentebale</a> (co-founded with <a href="/wiki/Prince_Seeiso_of_Lesotho" title="Prince Seeiso of Lesotho">Prince Seeiso of Lesotho</a>)</li>
<li>The Royal Foundation of The Duke and Duchess of Cambridge and Prince Harry (co-founded with his brother)</li>
<li>School's Games (President)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Invictus_Games_(multi-sport_event)" title="Invictus Games (multi-sport event)">Invictus Games</a> (President of the Invictus Games)<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>England Rugby 2015 (Honorary President). England Rugby 2015 is the organising committee delivering Rugby World Cup 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>As part of the Walking With The Wounded - South Pole Allied Challenge 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry became the first member of the royal family to reach the South Pole.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg/220px-Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg/330px-Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg/440px-Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2497" data-file-height="1666" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Henry_playing_volleyball.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harry talking to an opponent during a volleyball competition between American and British injured soldiers, 13 May 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harry enjoys playing many sporting activities, playing competitive <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">motocross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-POWInt_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POWInt-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Harry is a supporter of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal Football Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry is also a keen <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" title="Rugby Union" class="mw-redirect">Rugby Union</a> fan, and supported England's bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015 Rugby World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harry earned a reputation in his youth for being rebellious, leading the <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_journalism" title="Tabloid journalism">tabloid</a> press to label him as a "wild child."<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> He was found at age 17 smoking <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> and partaking in under-age drinking with his friends, clashing physically with <a href="/wiki/Paparazzi" title="Paparazzi">paparazzi</a> outside nightclubs,<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and was photographed at <a href="/wiki/Highgrove_House" title="Highgrove House">Highgrove House</a> at a "Colonial and Native" themed <a href="/wiki/Costume_party" title="Costume party">costume party</a> wearing a Nazi <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Afrika_Korps" title="Afrika Korps">Afrika Korps</a> uniform with a <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastika</a> armband.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> He later issued a public statement apologising for his behaviour.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2009, the British <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid</a> <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i> revealed a video made by Harry three years earlier in which he referred to a Pakistani fellow officer cadet as "our little <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_slurs#Paki" title="List of ethnic slurs">Paki</a> friend" and later called a soldier wearing a cloth on his head a "<a href="/wiki/Raghead" title="Raghead" class="mw-redirect">raghead</a>". These terms were described by <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> as "unacceptable",<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphy_on_harry_comments_2009_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphy_on_harry_comments_2009-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> as "racist",<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphy_on_harry_comments_2009_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphy_on_harry_comments_2009-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and a British Muslim youth organisation called Harry a "thug".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clarence_House" title="Clarence House">Clarence House</a> immediately issued an apology from Harry, who stated that no malice was intended in his remarks.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-100"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> A former British MP and Royal Marine, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Richards" title="Rod Richards">Rod Richards</a>, said that such nicknames were common amongst military comrades, stating "in the Armed Forces people often used to call me Taffy. Others were called Yankie, Oz or Kiwi or whatever. I consider Paki as an abbreviation for Pakistani. I don't think on this occasion it was intended to be offensive."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While on holiday in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> in August 2012, Harry and an unknown young woman were photographed naked in a <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Las_Vegas" title="Wynn Las Vegas">Wynn Las Vegas</a> hotel room, reportedly during a game of strip <a href="/wiki/Billiards" title="Billiards" class="mw-redirect">billiards</a>. The pictures were leaked by American celebrity website <a href="/wiki/TMZ_(website)" title="TMZ (website)" class="mw-redirect">TMZ</a> on 21 August,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> being reported worldwide by mainstream media on 22 August.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The photographs were shown by the American media, but British media were reluctant to publish them<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> – royal aides suggested that <a href="/wiki/Clarence_House" title="Clarence House">Clarence House</a> may contact the <a href="/wiki/Press_Complaints_Commission" title="Press Complaints Commission">Press Complaints Commission</a> (PCC) if the pictures are used by British publications.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_Palace" title="St James's Palace">St James's Palace</a> confirmed that Harry was in the photographs, said that he was essentially a victim of <a href="/wiki/Sexting" title="Sexting">sexting</a> in a private moment, and contacted the <a href="/wiki/Press_Complaints_Commission" title="Press Complaints Commission">Press Complaints Commission</a> upon hearing that a number of British newspapers were considering publishing the photographs.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> On 24 August <a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)"><i>The Sun</i></a> newspaper published photographs.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Polls conducted in the United Kingdom in November 2012 showed Harry to be the third most popular member of the Royal Family, after William and the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Rumours have persisted that Harry might be the son of <a href="/wiki/James_Hewitt" title="James Hewitt">James Hewitt</a>, with whom his mother had an affair, but this has been refuted by Hewitt and others, who point out that Harry was born before the affair began.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>fn 2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chelsy_Davy" title="Chelsy Davy">Chelsy Davy</a>, the daughter of a South African businessperson Charles Davy, was referred to as Harry's girlfriend in an interview conducted for his 21st birthday, and Harry said he "would love to tell everyone how amazing she is but once I start talking about that, I have left myself open...There is truth and there is lies and unfortunately I cannot get the truth across."<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 2009, it was reported in the media that the pair had parted ways after knowing each other for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> During the relationship, Davy was present as Harry received his Operational Service Medal for Afghanistan<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleMedal_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleMedal-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> and also attended Prince Harry's graduation ceremony when he received his flying wings from his father.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Daily_Telegraph_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Daily_Telegraph-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harry was introduced to girlfriend Cressida Bonas, granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Curzon,_6th_Earl_Howe" title="Edward Curzon, 6th Earl Howe">Edward Curzon, 6th Earl Howe</a>, by his cousin <a href="/wiki/Princess_Eugenie_of_York" title="Princess Eugenie of York">Princess Eugenie</a> in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Bonas accompanied Harry to an official engagement for the first time in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> On 30 April 2014 it was announced that the couple had parted amicably.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles.2C_styles.2C_honours_and_arms">Titles, styles, honours and arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Titles, styles, honours and arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_styles">Titles and styles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Titles and styles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg/170px-Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg.png" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg/255px-Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg/340px-Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="283" data-file-height="419" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Monogram_of_Prince_Harry_of_Wales.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal monogram</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harry's full style and title is <i>His Royal Highness Prince Henry Charles Albert David of Wales</i>, but he is informally known as Prince Harry. He uses the name of the area over which his father holds title, i.e., <i>Wales</i>, as a territorial suffix in lieu of surname. Past precedent is that such surnames are dropped from usage in adulthood, after which either title alone or <a href="/wiki/Mountbatten-Windsor" title="Mountbatten-Windsor">Mountbatten-Windsor</a> is used when necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Harry continues to use Wales as his surname for military purposes and is known as Captain Harry Wales in such contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Traditionally, sons of the reigning monarch and of the Prince of Wales receive a dukedom immediately prior to marriage, the most recent being <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William</a>, who received the dukedom of <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Duke of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>.</p>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="450" /></a></span> <b>13 April 2008&#160;– 16 April 2011</b>: <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Lieutenant (British Army and Royal Marines)">Lieutenant</a>, The Blues and Royals<sup id="cite_ref-LG_15_April_2008_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LG_15_April_2008-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_British_Army.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="450" /></a></span> <b>16 April 2011&#160;– Present</b>: <a href="/wiki/Captain_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Captain (British Army and Royal Marines)">Captain</a>, The Blues and Royals</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Appointments">Appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<dl>
<dt><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> Canada</dt>

</dl>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg/23px-Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg/35px-Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg/46px-Ensign_of_the_Royal_Air_Force.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="1800" /></a></span> <b>3 October 2008&#160;– present</b>: Honorary Air Commandant of <a href="/wiki/RAF_Honington" title="RAF Honington">RAF Honington</a><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Naval_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="360" /></a></span> <b>8 August 2006&#160;– present</b>: <a href="/wiki/Commodore-in-Chief" title="Commodore-in-Chief">Commodore-in-Chief</a> of Small Ships and Diving<sup id="cite_ref-POWReg_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POWReg-123"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_awards">Humanitarian awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Humanitarian awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Harry has twice had his charitable efforts recognised by the international community. In December 2010, the German charity <i>Ein Herz für Kinder</i> ("Heart for Children") awarded him the Golden Heart Award, in recognition of his "charitable and humanitarian efforts".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>19 December 2010: Golden Heart Award</li>
<li>7 May 2012: <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Council" title="Atlantic Council">Atlantic Council</a>'s Distinguished Humanitarian Leadership Award<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: 100%">
<caption>Arms of Prince Harry</caption>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Henry of Wales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg/220px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg.png" width="220" height="206" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg/330px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg/440px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Henry_of_Wales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1430" /></a></td>
<td>
<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
<dd>On his 18th birthday, Harry was granted his own personal <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">arms of the sovereign in right of the United Kingdom</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> for difference.</dd>
<dt>Adopted</dt>
<dd>15 September 2002</dd>
<dt>Escutcheon</dt>
<dd>Quarterly 1st and 4th gules three lions passant guardant in pale or armed and langed azure 2nd or a lion rampant gules armed and langued azure within a double tressure flory counterflory of the second 3rd azure a harp or stringed argent</dd>
<dt>Supporters</dt>
<dd>Dexter a lion rampant gardant Or imperially crowned proper, sinister a unicorn argent, armed, crined and unguled Or, gorged with a coronet Or composed of crosses patée and fleurs de lis a chain affixed thereto passing between the forelegs and reflexed over the back also Or.</dd>
<dt>Other elements</dt>
<dd>The whole differenced by a Label of five points Argent the first, third and fifth points charged with an Escallop Gules</dd>
<dt>Symbolism</dt>
<dd>As he is the grandchild of the sovereign, Harry's coat of arms has a label of five points. The <i>escallops</i> (seashells) allude to his mother Diana, Princess of Wales, whose <a href="/wiki/Earl_Spencer_(peerage)" title="Earl Spencer (peerage)">Spencer</a> coat of arms includes three <i>escallops argent</i>.</dd>
</dl>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Harry is a <a href="/wiki/Male_line" title="Male line" class="mw-redirect">male line</a> descendant of <a href="/wiki/Elimar_I,_Count_of_Oldenburg" title="Elimar I, Count of Oldenburg">Elimar I, Count of Oldenburg</a> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Oldenburg" title="House of Oldenburg">House of Oldenburg</a>, one of Europe's oldest royal houses, and the <a href="/wiki/Cadet_branch" title="Cadet branch">cadet branch</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Gl%C3%BCcksburg" title="House of Glücksburg">House of Glücksburg</a>, founded by his paternal ancestor <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm,_Duke_of_Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Gl%C3%BCcksburg" title="Friedrich Wilhelm, Duke of Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg">Friedrich Wilhelm, Duke of Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg</a>. His paternal grandmother issued <a href="/wiki/House_of_Windsor#Descendants_of_Elizabeth_II" title="House of Windsor">letters patent on 8 February 1960</a> declaring Harry's future father to be a member of the United Kingdom's reigning House of Windsor and a bearer of its name. Their male line <a href="/wiki/House_of_Oldenburg" title="House of Oldenburg">House of Oldenburg</a> ancestors include five Danish kings — <a href="/wiki/Christian_I_of_Denmark" title="Christian I of Denmark">Christian I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Denmark" title="Frederick I of Denmark">Frederick I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_III_of_Denmark" title="Christian III of Denmark">Christian III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_IX_of_Denmark" title="Christian IX of Denmark">Christian IX</a> - King <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Greece" title="George I of Greece">George I of Greece</a>, 11 <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Oldenburg" title="Count of Oldenburg" class="mw-redirect">counts of Oldenburg</a>, two dukes of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg" title="Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg">Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg</a>, five dukes of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Beck" title="Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Beck">Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Beck</a> and one duke of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Gl%C3%BCcksburg" title="Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg" class="mw-redirect">Schleswig-Holstein-Sonderburg-Glücksburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among his other recent ancestors on his father's side are members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Battenberg" title="House of Battenberg" class="mw-redirect">House of Battenberg</a>, the main line of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hesse-Darmstadt" title="House of Hesse-Darmstadt" class="mw-redirect">House of Hesse-Darmstadt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="House of Hesse-Kassel" class="mw-redirect">House of Hesse-Kassel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern" title="House of Hohenzollern">House of Hohenzollern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Among his distant ancestors are <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_England" title="Henry IV of England">Henry IV</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James II and VII</a>. Through his father's royal family, Harry is of German,<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> English and Scottish descent, and through his mother's family, the <a href="/wiki/Earl_Spencer_(peerage)" title="Earl Spencer (peerage)">Earl Spencer</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baron_Fermoy" title="Baron Fermoy">Baron Fermoy</a> families, of English descent and of remote German, Irish, Scottish and <a href="/wiki/British-American" title="British-American" class="mw-redirect">British-American</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-williamson_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williamson-128"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="navbox collapsible collapsed uncollapsed" style="width:100%; clear:none;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Harry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-sur-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sur_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sur_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Prince Harry does not normally use a surname, but when one is required, it may be <a href="/wiki/Mountbatten-Windsor" title="Mountbatten-Windsor">Mountbatten-Windsor</a>. In his military career, Harry uses the surname <i>Wales</i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The rumours are supposedly based on a similarity of hair colour; however, red hair is a known Spencer family trait. Hewitt told the press in 2002, "There really is no possibility whatsoever that I am Harry's father. I can absolutely assure you that I am not…I can understand the interest but Harry was already walking by the time my relationship with Diana began. Admittedly the red hair is similar to mine and people say we look alike. I have never encouraged these comparisons and although I was with Diana for a long time I must state once and for all that I'm not Harry's father." This was corroborated by Diana's police bodyguard.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
